Now I can see the real issue! The problem is that node-sass@4.14.1 requires Python to build native bindings, but Python is not available in the Alpine Linux container. The node-sass package is quite old and has compatibility issues with newer Node.js versions.

Let me fix this by updating the Dockerfile to install Python and build tools, and also suggest updating to a more modern CSS preprocessor:

Accepted edits to

Dockerfile

docker-compose build --no-cache web-test-tool

Perfect! Now I can see the issue clearly. The backend is trying to connect to MySQL using the hostname mysql, but when running the container standalone (not through docker-compose), it can't resolve that hostname. This is expected behavior - the backend needs to be part of the Docker network to connect to the MySQL service.

The issue is that the backend container is failing its health check because it can't connect to MySQL during startup. Let me check the docker-compose configuration to see if we need to adjust the startup order or health checks.

Dockerfile

Kiro
I can see the issue now! Redis is failing to start because of a configuration error. The error message shows:

*** FATAL CONFIG FILE ERROR (Redis 6.2.20) ***
Reading the configuration file, at line 3
>>> 'requirepass'
wrong number of arguments
This means there's an issue with the Redis configuration file. The requirepass directive is missing its password value. Let me check the Redis configuration:

Read file(s)

docker-compose.yml 20 - 51
Found the issue! The Redis command is using --requirepass ${REDIS_PASSWORD:-} but when REDIS_PASSWORD is empty (which it is by default), it becomes --requirepass with no value, which is invalid syntax.

Let me check the .env file to see what's set:

Read file(s)

.env
The REDIS_PASSWORD is empty. I need to fix the docker-compose.yml to handle the case when Redis password is empty. Let me update it:
